For anyone considering watching the movie Civil War. This is my POV: It's trash. It promotes hate speech, discrimination, and violence.  It promotes violence against the POTUS.   The Civil War movie promotes Hate Speech and Violence. The movie crosses several lines by promoting hate speech, discrimination, and explicit violence. It goes as far as to suggest violence against the President of the United States, which is not only irresponsible but also dangerous in our current socio-political climate. Journalists are portrayed unrealistically. Journalists are depicted as heroes facing extreme threats, including being shot on sight if they attempt to enter the White House. This portrayal seems exaggerated and unrealistic, undermining the film's credibility. Negative Portrayal of Military and Police. The US military and police are cast as antagonists. Their representation is unfair and biased. The movie fails to acknowledge the complexities and sacrifices of these professions, instead opting for a simplistic and negative portrayal. Graphic and Disturbing Violence. One of the most disturbing scenes involves an African American being restrained, doused in accelerant, and burned alive. This graphic depiction of violence is not only horrifying but also seems gratuitous and exploitative. Currency and Cultural Missteps. The preference for Canadian currency over US dollars is an absurd and unrealistic detail that further detracts from the film's believability. Additionally, rural Americans are stereotyped as hillbillies engaging in price gouging and hanging civilians, which is both offensive and reductive. Misogynistic Depictions. Male characters in the film are overwhelmingly portrayed as misogynists, which feels like a lazy stereotype rather than any meaningful commentary on the dynamics of male/female psychology. Antifa as Victims. The movie paints Antifa members as victims of a massacre, which again lacks believability and comes off as a one-sided narrative. This portrayal feels like an attempt to push a specific political agenda rather than provide a balanced view. Poor Production Quality. On a technical level, the film is riddled with poorly constructed sets and fake-looking scenes. The low production quality only adds to the overall sense of disbelief and frustration. Overall Civil War comes across as a sick fantasy pandering to a Progressive Liberal agenda. It depicts a dystopian world where civilians form rogue militias to assassinate people of color, ethnic minorities, and non-Americans. The narrative is extreme and disconnected from reality. Civil War is a film that I found to be deeply flawed and problematic. Its promotion of hate, graphic violence, and one-sided political messaging makes it a troubling watch. If you're looking for a balanced and thoughtful film, this is not it.

But I do hope there was written a hopeful way out in this film; perhaps a serious attempt at rooting out the core of our troubles. For example, might we learn why so many Americans feel so deprived and miserable when we have long been the richest nation on Earth?  Viewed from a historical perspective of the last 75 years or so, one must assume we Americans shouldn't have much to worry about; that there is plenty to share and be thankful for.  So why civil war? Why even bring it up? A civil war doesn't make any sense when our people have long been well-fed, well-housed and enjoy material conveniences that many around the world can only dream about. Why should otherwise normal people become to so irritable and unhappy when we are known to have the best schools and the best medicines, the best technology and the best hospitals on Earth?   What could it possibly be that underlies the frustration, the anger, suspicion and mistrust that would move us toward a civil war? Is it because of something we can't see, feel or taste? Could it be something systemic, some defect. Some inherent flaw?  Why are we even thinking about civil war, anyway?  .

The Civil War was fought in 10,000 places, from Val Verde, New Mexico, and Tullahoma, Tennessee, to St. Albans, Vermont, and Fernandina on the Florida coast. More than 3 million Americans fought in it, and over 600,000 men, 2 percent of the population, died in it.  American homes became headquarters. American churches and schoolhouses sheltered the dying, and huge foraging armies swept across American farms, burned American towns, Americans slaughtered one another wholesale, right here in America, in their own cornfields and peach orchards, along familiar roads and by waters with old American names. In two days at Shiloh, on the banks of the Tennessee River, more American men fell than an all previous American wars combined. At Cold Harbor, some 7,000 American fell in twenty minutes. Men who had never strayed twenty miles from their own front doors now found themselves soldiers in great armies fighting epic battles hundreds of miles from home. They knew they were making history, and it was the greatest adventure of their lives. The Civil War has been given many names: the War Between the States, the War Against Northern Aggression, the Second American Revolution, the Lost Cause, the War of the Rebellion, the Brothers War, the Late Unpleasantness.   Walt Whitman called it the War of Attempted Secession. Between 1861 and 1865, Americans made war on each other and killed each other in great numbers - if only to become the kind of country that could no longer conceive of how that was possible. What began as a bitter dispute over Union and States Rights, ended as a struggle over the meaning of freedom in America.
